  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_902aedd1-18cc-46c2-9481-03fbae4cb833'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer6457152448356271215">Just before summer begins, 13-year-old Ali finds an odd photograph in the attic. She knows the two children in it are her mother, Claire, and her aunt Dulcie. But who’s the third person, the one who’s been torn out of the picture?<br/><br/>Ali figures she’ll find out while she’s vacationing in Maine with Dulcie and her four-year-old daughter, Emma, in the house where Ali’s mother’s </span>
  <span id="freeText6457152448356271215" style="display:none">Just before summer begins, 13-year-old Ali finds an odd photograph in the attic. She knows the two children in it are her mother, Claire, and her aunt Dulcie. But who’s the third person, the one who’s been torn out of the picture?<br /><br />Ali figures she’ll find out while she’s vacationing in Maine with Dulcie and her four-year-old daughter, Emma, in the house where Ali’s mother’s family used to spend summers. All hopes for relaxation are quashed shortly after their arrival, though, when the girls meet Sissy, a kid who’s mean and spiteful and a bad influence on Emma.<br /><br />Strangest of all, Sissy keeps talking about a girl named Teresa who drowned under mysterious circumstances back when Claire and Dulcie were kids, and whose body was never found. At first Ali thinks Sissy’s just trying to scare her with a ghost story, but soon she discovers the real reason why Sissy is so angry. . . . Mary Downing Hahn is at her chilling best in this new supernatural tale that’s certain to send shivers down her readers’ spines.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1768611749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7575951507577005717">
  <b>
    <i>“The lake's deep...and dark...and dangerous.” </i>
  </b>
<br/><br/>You can find this review and all of my other reviews at <a href='http://www.noveldescent.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Novel Descent</a> Thanks for the support!<br/><br/>I originally rated this three stars but after rowing it over in my mind I had to drop this one down to one star. There was some very problematic issues with the characters and there was one sentence in the book that made my mouth drop, due to racism. <br/><br/><i>Deep and Dark and Dangerous</i> is about a young girl who is 13 who goes to stay with her aunt and her</span>
  <span id="freeText7575951507577005717" style="display:none">
  <b>
    <i>“The lake's deep...and dark...and dangerous.” </i>
  </b>
<br /><br />You can find this review and all of my other reviews at <a href="http://www.noveldescent.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Descent</a> Thanks for the support!<br /><br />I originally rated this three stars but after rowing it over in my mind I had to drop this one down to one star. There was some very problematic issues with the characters and there was one sentence in the book that made my mouth drop, due to racism. <br /><br /><i>Deep and Dark and Dangerous</i> is about a young girl who is 13 who goes to stay with her aunt and her little cousin for the summer at a family summer home. Her aunt and her siblings haven't been to the house since they were little and they avoid all questions about why they won't go to the house. As soon as they arrive at the summer home another young girl named Sissy starts turning up out of nowhere and wanting to play. This puts the girls in numerous awkward or dangerous situations, not to mention their moods change when they are around her. <br /><br />Ok, I might as well address the elephant in the room right away. Was this book racist? Well, I wouldn't go as far as to say it was a racist book but I would say there was a very good example of casual racism within it. At one point the girls are playing on the beach and Sissy comes up behind them, the girls remark how they did not hear her coming. Her response is and I quote, "I sneaked up on you, I'm as quiet as an Indian." (It was on page 76 in my edition, incase you want to look at it for yourself.)<br /><br />Now let's get into why this is so problematic. Obviously the comment in itself is pretty racist, referring to the idea that Indians are sneaky. Next, there is NO reason for the comment. This is probably the biggest issue about this. The character is not racist, there is no signs, other than that one throw-a-way comment that they are racist. There is nothing about race in the book and it had nothing to do with anything that was going on. Do I think the author was racist? I really can't answer that question because I haven't read enough of her work and in the other book I read I didn't particularly notice anything. When I first read the sentence that I'm referring to, I kind of slowly stopped and thought, "there is no way I just read that." So, I read it over a few times, looked for some way that I could explain away the racism then I shrugged and figured that this must be a book of its era. I guessed this book to be written maybe in the 50s-70s at the latest. It read like an older book and the cover suggested it as well, so I checked the year. Wrong again, it was published in 2007 *bangs head on desk* How it got past the editors I'll never know. There is just no excuse in the year 2007 to have such stereotypical racism in a book. I personally would have an issue allowing children I know to read this without proper context. It is normalizing racism. Not a good thing in my book. I know some people may roll their eyes at the amount of content I'm writing on this, but I think it's important that we talk about these things when we see them. <br /><br />Another huge issue with this book is the characters. None of them are particularly likeable. The protagonist isn't awful but there's nothing special about her, the little girl she babysits for is one of the most annoying children I have read about in a long time and Sissy (the mysterious girl) is just a complete monster of a character, not in a good way. The adults are harsh, and when they have their more tender moments it's still hard not to think of them as complete batshit crazy morons. I just couldn't get on board with any of them. <br /><br />Is there anything really positive about this book? I thought I liked it at first but I realized I liked the feeling of it. It felt like an older story and it gave me a cozy feeling. I was letting a lot of things slide because of that. <br /><br />I did read Mary Downing Hahn' more known book <i>Wait Till Helen Comes</i> and enjoyed it much more. I will read more of her books and hope that I do not come into these issues again. I can't in my right mind recommend a book like this though.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7575951507577005717" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16414237528329353405" style="display:none">blech.<br /><br />so, here is this book in a nutshell:<br /><br /><br />claire: no, you can't go to the beach house! it's bad! water is bad! everything is bad! ouch! my head hurts!<br />ali: mom, you're, like, soooo over-protective!<br />pete: ali, you can go!<br />dulcie: ali, you will serve as my 13yr old au pair all summer. in return, you will have all your emotional needs ignored and i will have all the time in the world to paint creepy pictures of the lake in my studio.<br />emma: i'm lonely!<br />sissy: i'm cold and lonely. and dead. come play with me. forever, and ever, and ever.<br />ali: aunt dulcie, is there something you want to tell us?<br />dulcie: no! you ingrate! how dare you?!?!<br />ali: guess i'll go read [To Kill a Mockingbird]<br />sissy: bury me or else!<br />ali: i think we should do what she says. but first, let me yell at her like i'm 7 and storm off like i'm 17.<br />dulcie: you rotten brat! how dare you!!! <br />emma: i'm lonely!<br />sissy: i just want a friend. and a funeral. is that too much to ask? oh, hey, a canoe!<br />ali: um...i really think we should tell someone about this deep dark secret you've been harboring for decades...<br />dulcie: fine. i'll call the police. and the newspapers. and my lawyer. and your mother.<br />sissy: yay! i'm finally free!<br />dulcie: yay! i'm finally free!<br />claire: yay! i'm finally free!<br />emma: i'm still lonely.<br /><br /><br />blech.<br /><br />there's virtually no mystery, the adults are all one-dimensional, the children are barely 2-d, and most of the characters are just so whiny or awful to like. what's up with parents being completely irrational and horrible people in these books? troubled, sure, that's forgivable, but irrevocably broken and cruel is problematic. <br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer17676936" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17387338754977556673">Ali is invited to spend the summer at the family’s old cottage up in Maine, watching her four-year-old niece Emma for her aunt Dulcie. But Ali’s mom is dead against it, saying the lake is too dangerous, and that it’s a dark and rainy place to have a miserable summer. She refuses to talk about her own childhood there, or who the third girl in the old photo Ali finds of her mom and Dulcie as kids at the lake. <br/>But Dulcie and Ali wear her down, and Ali goes off to Maine, where she finds her mother w</span>
  <span id="freeText17387338754977556673" style="display:none">Ali is invited to spend the summer at the family’s old cottage up in Maine, watching her four-year-old niece Emma for her aunt Dulcie. But Ali’s mom is dead against it, saying the lake is too dangerous, and that it’s a dark and rainy place to have a miserable summer. She refuses to talk about her own childhood there, or who the third girl in the old photo Ali finds of her mom and Dulcie as kids at the lake. <br />But Dulcie and Ali wear her down, and Ali goes off to Maine, where she finds her mother was right. The weather is rainy, cold and depressing. But worse than that is Sissy, a local girl who influences Emma into bratty, and risky, behavior. Sissy hints that she knows all about the girl in the photo, and what happened years ago that no one else will talk about, but Ali doesn’t trust her. <br />Creepy and very dark, the atmosphere of dread in this book seems to poison the behavior of the characters. Elements such as an old doll and mossy tombstones heighten the tension along the way to the inevitable conclusion. You may not have fun reading this, but you will get chills.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17387338754977556673" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1384646-jen-lohf-book-den?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer12886618330544085964">What a perfect book to read on the heels of reading Violet by Scott Thomas! This book could have easily been his inspiration behind writing Violet.<br/><br/>Deep and Dark and Dangerous is a middle grade ghost story. I really enjoyed the ghosty bits of this one. It's a great book for young horror lovers. I would have loved it back in my Lois Duncan days!<br/><br/>Unfortunately, the characters didn't always work well for me. The main character is Ali, and she often flipped from being mature to acting like a young chi</span>
  <span id="freeText12886618330544085964" style="display:none">What a perfect book to read on the heels of reading Violet by Scott Thomas! This book could have easily been his inspiration behind writing Violet.<br /><br />Deep and Dark and Dangerous is a middle grade ghost story. I really enjoyed the ghosty bits of this one. It's a great book for young horror lovers. I would have loved it back in my Lois Duncan days!<br /><br />Unfortunately, the characters didn't always work well for me. The main character is Ali, and she often flipped from being mature to acting like a young child. This is probably true to life, but I think middle grade readers would appreciate spending time with her more than I did. I didn't find the 6 year old character to be very realistic either, but I'm not exactly the intended audience.<br /><br />If you are looking for a spooky story set on the lake, Deep and Dark and Dangerous is a quick (and younger) ghostly tale.</span>

<div id="review_21522606" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/21522606" />
    <a title="Tina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/817311-tina"><img alt="Tina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1228787000p2/817311.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/21522606?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tina" href="/user/show/817311-tina">Tina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21522606" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2918195608350343897">This book was a wonderful story. There was so much that you could get from it. There was happiness, horror, and laughter all mixed in. Also some sadness. The creepiness of the story brought among the main suspense of the story along with the mystery of the new characters and new conflicts. During some times i felt like popping into the book and dealing with the situations myself since i felt they were not strongly dealt with although that was probably the author's point to make sure the story co</span>
  <span id="freeText2918195608350343897" style="display:none">This book was a wonderful story. There was so much that you could get from it. There was happiness, horror, and laughter all mixed in. Also some sadness. The creepiness of the story brought among the main suspense of the story along with the mystery of the new characters and new conflicts. During some times i felt like popping into the book and dealing with the situations myself since i felt they were not strongly dealt with although that was probably the author's point to make sure the story continues at a fast pace. The story more than being a scare your socks of story is a delicate horror story woven to expose the personality of Sassy and how the book can be scary even without monsters, and goblins and etc. The book wasn't at all predictable and even left a couple of red herrings. I loved the ending. Peace and happiness are two good ways to end a story based on my opinion and Mary Downing Hahn incorporated both those elements into the ending of the story which even brought an extent of tears to my eyes. A book I recommend to all for its uniqueness and plot. Enjoy!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2918195608350343897" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_70857260" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/70857260" />
    <a title="Natalie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2728338-natalie"><img alt="Natalie" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/70857260?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie" href="/user/show/2728338-natalie">Natalie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer70857260" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1166393893553411590">This book, Deep and Dark and Dangerous is about a girl named Ali who finds an old photograph of three kids one is her mom the other is her aunt Dulcie but the third person is torn from the picture. Ali has about 2 months to figure out who the third person is because she is spending that time in a beach house her mom and aunt used to stay in when they were kids. Ali wanted to go to the beach with her aunt because she wanted to babysit her little cousin and she wanted to find out who the third per</span>

Ali has about 2 months to figure out who the third person is because she is spending that time in a beach house her mom and aunt used to stay in when they were kids.   <span id="freeText15591674573252252238" style="display:none">Deep and Dark and Dangerous is fiction and mystery is a really good book and the story takes place in Main. <br /><br />The main character Ali is a young girl who lives her mom and dad but her mom has so issues she gets upset about everything and she gets this migraines and she is always locked up in her room when she has the migraines. her dad is very nice and he is a hardworking man who loves ali very much. One day when Ali was looking around in the attic she finds this old picture and she recognizes her mom Claire and her aunt Dulcie when they were kids but also she noticed that there was another girl to the other side of her mom but that part of the picture was torn and all she could see was part of the hand and in the back the letter T. Days later her aunt came over and ask Ali to go with her to the lake where she and her mom just to go in the summer when they were little Ali was so exited and she really wanted to go. Sissy was a mean selfish girl at first she was nice to Emma and Ali but then she would get mean with then she was very mysterious. Sissy then became a bad influence for Emma because since she started to hangout with Sissy, Emma started to change she wasn't the nice girl anymore she would blame Ali for Everything and say that Ali wanted to hurt her and that she was mean to her.     <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1289721096" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1289721096" />
    <a title="Eugene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11137617-eugene"><img alt="Eugene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442520750p2/11137617.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1289721096?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eugene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eugene" href="/user/show/11137617-eugene">Eugene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1289721096" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3934871245052393927">A surprisingly disappointing entry from a normally reliable author. It seems a rewrite of a her wonderful <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/267972.Wait_Till_Helen_Comes' title='Wait Till Helen Comes by Mary Downing Hahn' rel='nofollow noopener'>Wait Till Helen Comes</a>, with many of the same tropes. But the protagonist is paper-thin, nothing much to her to appeal, and the story relies on the Stupidity Plot Drive. A story that is advanced only by the hero's incapacity to think of the obvious solution is painful. It's one thing when a thirteen year-old girl lets herself be putty in a malicious eleven year-old's hands. Such things happen</span>
  <span id="freeText3934871245052393927" style="display:none">A surprisingly disappointing entry from a normally reliable author. It seems a rewrite of a her wonderful <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/267972.Wait_Till_Helen_Comes" title="Wait Till Helen Comes by Mary Downing Hahn" rel="nofollow noopener">Wait Till Helen Comes</a>, with many of the same tropes. But the protagonist is paper-thin, nothing much to her to appeal, and the story relies on the Stupidity Plot Drive. A story that is advanced only by the hero's incapacity to think of the obvious solution is painful. It's one thing when a thirteen year-old girl lets herself be putty in a malicious eleven year-old's hands. Such things happen, but, unless I have real reason to want to sympathize with the older girl, it does raise the question--so, would this ghost be dangerous if confronted with a mildly competent girl? Being manipulated by unbridled malice is one thing, but not knowing to hold tightly to her 4 year-old cousin the <i>second time</i> the ghost tells her to do something dangerous; not thinking to bodily lift the 4 year-old out of the canoe when she knows the ghost intends to sink her... this is a level of incompetence that strains credibility.<br /><br />Otherwise, both the supporting characters undergo radical shifts of mood, from loving devotion to malicious attack, so extreme I was forced to believe they were being possessed by the ghost. Then the protagonist suddenly changes her mind about the ghost and is her best friend, for no discernible reason. The story feels long and drawn out, having its climax near the middle, and then meandering around the relationships of these incomprehensible characters. It's wordy, too. When it was time to say, "It said 'Theresa,'" because the reader already knows, instead we get: "Then I saw the name. Five more sentences. I couldn't believe it. More words. It was the girl from the canoe, the girl who'd been bothering us all this time, the girl you knew from the get-go was the ghost, Theresa."<br /><br />In "Wait Till Helen Comes" Hahn deftly managed the push and pull of the mean girl, the discovery of the truth, and the transition of the relationship from fear and rejection to compassion. Read that and skip this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3934871245052393927" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1128337145" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1128337145" />
    <a title="Margaux Collier" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37605528-margaux-collier"><img alt="Margaux Collier" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1128337145?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Margaux Collier" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Margaux Collier" href="/user/show/37605528-margaux-collier">Margaux Collier</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1128337145" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8022009844780117959">Deep and Dark and Dangerous, written by Mary Downing Hahn, is set in Dull Cottage in a village. The story is about a gril named Ali who while looking through books in the attic finds a torn photograph of her aunt, Dulcie and her mother. There is a personn standing next to her mum but that part has been torn off. At the back is written Dulcie, her mum's name and a 'T'. Ali goes to Dull Cottage with her cousin Emma and her aunt Dulcie. There she meets Sissy sho is mean and spiteful and is determin</span>
  <span id="freeText8022009844780117959" style="display:none">Deep and Dark and Dangerous, written by Mary Downing Hahn, is set in Dull Cottage in a village. The story is about a gril named Ali who while looking through books in the attic finds a torn photograph of her aunt, Dulcie and her mother. There is a personn standing next to her mum but that part has been torn off. At the back is written Dulcie, her mum's name and a 'T'. Ali goes to Dull Cottage with her cousin Emma and her aunt Dulcie. There she meets Sissy sho is mean and spiteful and is determined to ruin Ali's vacation. Sissy was really a dead girl's ghodt. She tells them a story about two sisters who had drowned a girl called Teresa. She starts possessing Emma and Ali soon realizes that Sissy is Teresa's ghost and the two sisters are her aunt and her mother. After going though all these problems, Ali tells Sissy that she has to go forever and that they don't want her back. Sissy, for the first time listens to Ali and leaves without any goodbyes or reasons. The theme of the story is friendship and revenge. Ali learns that revenge doesn't serve any good purpose. <br /><br />The main element of fiction in this book is suspense because whe you start reading, you can't close the book. "The lake's deep... and dark.. and dangerous" (Downing Hahn p.80" This quotes was suspensful because it shows how the author describe the lake. It makes the readerwonder what is so dangerous about this lake and wants to read on. Another suspensful part in the book was when Dulcie finds a message on the wall saying "Bones, Bones, you better die". Now it is easy to imagine how scary this message is. "The ghost is very sad and lonley. She wants to go home, but she's down deep, deep, deep in the water. She's been there so long,she's just bones. No one knows where she is" (Downing Hahn p.26) This quote really makes the story suspensful because we can see how the author tries to scare the reader in this quote. This elemnt of fiction suspense makes the book very interesting because once the reader starts reading; the reader can't close the book. <br /><br />I would recommend this book to any gender. I would recommend this book because if you like scary books then you should read this one. Another reason is because the character, Ali is smart and manages to find everything out without help from anyone. Finally, the theme is very exiting. As one can see, Deep and Dark and Dangerous is onsidered to be very exiting because of the suspense in this book </span>

<div id="review_205760480" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/205760480" />
    <a title="Stacie N" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5031390-stacie-n"><img alt="Stacie N" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1315316504p2/5031390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/205760480?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacie N" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacie N" href="/user/show/5031390-stacie-n">Stacie N</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer205760480" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16686101430379861694">"That lake is deep and dark and dangerous..." <br/><br/> Suspenseful and eerie, Deep and Dark and Dangerous will surely leave you on edge. <br/> Thirteen year old Ali finds an old photo of her mother, Claire, and Aunt Dulcie at Gull Cottage, their lake house...but there's another girl in the photo that was ripped out, merely left with the letter "T". Dulcie and Claire act like there never was a "T", but Ali knows something's up, so when overprotective Claire finally allows Ali to go to Gull Cottage with Dulcie</span>
  <span id="freeText16686101430379861694" style="display:none">"That lake is deep and dark and dangerous..." <br /><br /> Suspenseful and eerie, Deep and Dark and Dangerous will surely leave you on edge. <br /> Thirteen year old Ali finds an old photo of her mother, Claire, and Aunt Dulcie at Gull Cottage, their lake house...but there's another girl in the photo that was ripped out, merely left with the letter "T". Dulcie and Claire act like there never was a "T", but Ali knows something's up, so when overprotective Claire finally allows Ali to go to Gull Cottage with Dulcie and Emma, Claire's 5 year old niece, Ali is determined to find out more about "T" who they discover is "Teresa". But when the vandalism of Dulcie's art studio and the appearance of Sissy, a mean, spiteful girl determined to ruin Ali's summer and other strange events occur, Ali can't help but wonder who Teresa is. But the secrets may lie at the bottom of the deep, dark and dangerous lake.<br /> In the middle of the book, Emma would do everything Sissy told her to and was bullying her cousin, but Ali would still stand up for Emma. "'You're not fun, you're just a dumb copycat'" Sissy said in the book to Emma and Ali would come rushing to Emma's defense. I think it was really nice of Ali to stand up for Emma despite what she said to her earlier, but I probably wouldn't have done the same thing.<br /> In Deep and Dark and Dangerous, Ali stood up for Emma when Sissy repeatedly dunked Emma's head in the lake. That reminded me of the time I stood up for my sister at my cousin's birthday party when we were little kids. A boy a year older than her kicked her, and I marched straight up to him and screamed "Nobody kicks my sister!" After that, he made sure to steer clear of us. <br /> This book taught me that everything is not what it seems and that you shouldn't judge a book by its cover. <br /> Deep and Dark and Dangerous would be the best book I've read so far this year because it had me turning pages late at night. I really enjoyed how the author wrote this book; they added a few suspenseful details in each chapter that make you slowly grow more on edge. Also, another thing this book did was that it hooked me from the very beginning. I couldn't put it down and I’m sure you won’t be able to as well. I recommend this to readers 10 and up that are looking for a suspensful, not to scary story to read. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16686101430379861694" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText15548477973293573961" style="display:none">A picture from the past will get you wondering. If you did not know the people in it you would ask yourself, “who are these people?” You would also ask “What are they doing?” You may also ask “Where are they at?” Photographs get you thinking and wondering. That is exactly what happened to Ali in the story Deep and Dark and Dangerous. Mary Downing Hahn’s Deep and Dark and Dangerous amazed me with its eerie style and suspenseful story.<br /><br />The theme of the book is friendship and the truth. It teaches you that you can find friendship in the strangest of places. It also teaches you that with the truth everything is more simple. Lies just make confusion and anger. I love how Hahn always leaves you in suspense and thinking. Also, Hahn makes her characters very believable. Ali is exactly what you would think a thirteen-year-old would act. The story is set on a lake, in a lake house during Ali’s summer vacation.<br /><br />In Deep and Dark and Dangerous it all started with Ali finding an old photograph in an old book she found in the attic. She recognizes two people but the third person is cut out. The two she recognizes are her aunt and her mother. All Ali could make out was long hair and an arm. From that she could tell it was a girl. On the back of the photograph it said “Gull Cottage, 1977. Dulcie, Claire, and T-.” Ali wanted to find out who this ripped out girl was, and why she had been ripped out. Ali could not stop thinking about this “T-” girl. She did not know what she was getting herself into.<br /><br />Deep and Dark and Dangerous by Mary Downing Hahn is a great book and I recommend this book to anyone who likes books that keeps you in suspense and whoever loves to try to solve mysteries. This book does not just tell a story but you feel as if you are personally in the story.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15548477973293573961" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16971160728457196197" style="display:none">	This book, I founded on the store bookshelf, I was on sale and it was a horror story, thus I brought it. Ali, a girl who had a huge curiosity of figuring out the secret behind the ripped photo. This was a secret her mother and aunt both hold, they were taking a photo with this other girl. T…? Determined to know Ali risk her life by going to this place where her mother and her aunt used to visit when they are kids. Two months was all she had, to figure out the third person in the photo. Before she realizes, weird things are happening. Her cousin's continuous nightmares of bones beneath the wide lake and her mysterious friend, Sissy they met. She seen to contain a secret as well, will she be the key to all her questions?<br />Conflict:<br />	Teresa or sissy, does it matter? Sissy appears out in thin air and disappears in the matter of milliseconds, her constant spirit bothers Ali and her cousin, Emma when they are out of town for their summer vacation. Summer was suppose to be fun for them right, but they soon figure out Emma's first real friend was a ghost who wanted the truth. The secret between her mother and her aunt was suppose to be known, but they kept it as a secret, a secret that causes all the problems. For example, when suddenly there's a note saying, "'I'm watching you tell the truth or else" (Hahn 80).As Sissy desperately wanted the truth to be revealed, Ali and Emma helped her on the way. They two were mini- versions of their mother. After many attempts, at last sissy will finally rest in peace. "'In Memory of Our Beloved Daughter and Sister Teresa Abbott. May her soul rise from the deep and be at peace" (Hahn 123). Finally Ali and Emma can enjoy their summer together once again without the distraction of sissy, they are all in peace. <br /></span>

           <span class="uitext reviewText">Children 10-15. Lovers of horror, ghost stories, happy endings.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

<span id="freeTextContainer2286496124279246068"><p> 13 year old Ali has been invited by her aunt to spend the summer with her and her 5 year old daughter Emma at a cottage by a lake in Maine. Although her mother is reluctant to let her go, she eventually agrees. Ali keeps finding evidence of a little girl who was most likely her mom and aunt's friend and the only hint to her name is T from a torn photograph. But when she asks her mom and then her aunt about her. They both claim to have no memory of another girl. But Ali suspects they may not be </p></span>
  <span id="freeText2286496124279246068" style="display:none"><p> 13 year old Ali has been invited by her aunt to spend the summer with her and her 5 year old daughter Emma at a cottage by a lake in Maine. Although her mother is reluctant to let her go, she eventually agrees. Ali keeps finding evidence of a little girl who was most likely her mom and aunt's friend and the only hint to her name is T from a torn photograph. But when she asks her mom and then her aunt about her. They both claim to have no memory of another girl. But Ali suspects they may not be telling the truth.</p><br /><p> Ali's job is to babysit her younger cousin when your aunt is in her studio painting. A job Ali loves and she loves spending time with her cousin. A few days in they run into another little girl about 10 years old and her name is Sissy. Emma immediately wants to be Sissy's friend and starts acting just like her. Problem is Sissy acts like a brat and can be pretty mean at times. Ali tries to get more info out of Sissy about herself so she can find her parents and get Sissy to leave them be. But Sissy is secretive, sneaky, and possibly more than she appears to be. .</p><br /><p> It was cute ghost story. Spooky but not super scary. It had a happy ending too. I can see older children and younger teens really enjoying this story. There really is nothing about this book that I think is bad or inappropriate for the age of children capable of reading it. And while I was certainly to old for this particular story, even I found it to be entertaining. This the second book I have read by Mary Downing Hahn, and think she does a great job the audience she target. Books sometimes makes me the Goosebumps, but not in a copycat sense. She has her own originality to her work</p></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/74436333" />
    <a title="Jim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2193587-jim"><img alt="Jim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512022938p2/2193587.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/74436333?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim" href="/user/show/2193587-jim">Jim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer74436333" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7297461788529993639">Deep and Dark and Dangerous: A Ghost Story, by author Mary Downing Hahn, is a supernatural thriller that you may not want to read while you're alone... because if you do you'll probably just fall asleep. <br/><br/>Ali and Emma are two young cousins who are going to spend the summer together in their moms' old cabin in the mountains of Maine. Emma's mother, Dulcie, is the sister of Ali's mother, Claire. Dulcie is an artist who's seeking solitude from big city life so she can concentrate on her paintings. S</span>
  <span id="freeText7297461788529993639" style="display:none">Deep and Dark and Dangerous: A Ghost Story, by author Mary Downing Hahn, is a supernatural thriller that you may not want to read while you're alone... because if you do you'll probably just fall asleep. <br /><br />Ali and Emma are two young cousins who are going to spend the summer together in their moms' old cabin in the mountains of Maine. Emma's mother, Dulcie, is the sister of Ali's mother, Claire. Dulcie is an artist who's seeking solitude from big city life so she can concentrate on her paintings. She figures spending the summer in her childhood cabin is the perfect place to get some work done. She takes along her daughter Emma, and invites her niece Ali along as well. It's not long before Ali and Emma meet a stranger who begins to rattle and unnerve them with her strange, erratic behavior and grumblings of a secret that their mothers have been keeping from them. Ali and Emma experience intense moment after moment as they decide to pursue the truth about their mothers.<br /><br />Now I'll pursue the truth about this book. It's boring, predictable and like reading the diary of a 13 year old drama queen who does nothing but argue with her menopausal aunt, little brat cousin and a confused prepubescent ghost. Not a good story. However, I did find I needed much less Ambien during the agonizing month it took me to get through this. So there's something good.</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7519192-emily?shelf=reads2012">reads2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer306629629" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12443831040572630627">Emily Shepard<br/>Horror<br/>Thirteen year old Ali wants so badly to go to Maine for the summer. But her mother wanted her to be as far away from her families cottage in Maine as she possibly could. With lots of pleading from Alis' young cousin, Emma, and her Aunt Dulcie her mother reluctantly agreed. Ali was looking forward to spending the summer away from home and working for her aunt as Emma's babysitter. When they arrive everything was just as Aunt Dulcie had remembered, except for the name Teresa. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText12443831040572630627" style="display:none">Emily Shepard<br />Horror<br />Thirteen year old Ali wants so badly to go to Maine for the summer. But her mother wanted her to be as far away from her families cottage in Maine as she possibly could. With lots of pleading from Alis' young cousin, Emma, and her Aunt Dulcie her mother reluctantly agreed. Ali was looking forward to spending the summer away from home and working for her aunt as Emma's babysitter. When they arrive everything was just as Aunt Dulcie had remembered, except for the name Teresa. They find the name on a game board and on a torn picture of her aunt and mother. Ali soon realizes the whole island is hiding something and her mother and aunt play a large role in the secret. To top that mystery off Ali and Emma meet a young blonde girl on the beach, Sissy. The girl is mean to them and makes Emma behave just like her. She turns their summer upside down and makes everyone hate one another. Could Sissy be the link to the missing girl Teresa? It's up to Ali to find the mystery of this little Maine town.<br />I didn't particularly like this story. I thought the plot was too easy to figure out and the characters were hard to identify with. I would suggest this book to a young girl however who would like to try reading a ghost story for the first time. It isn't too scary and its a fast read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12443831040572630627" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/611309317" />
    <a title="Lauren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13202240-lauren"><img alt="Lauren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393772906p2/13202240.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/611309317?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren" href="/user/show/13202240-lauren">Lauren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer611309317" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16392762956701935106">Deep Dark and Dangerous by Mary Downing Hahn is an excellent book if you're interested in paranormal books! It all started when the main character Ali was looking through her mom's old photographs. She finds a photo of her mother and siblings but then notices, there is someone ripped out of the photo. When Ali asks her mom, her mom acts as if she doesn't know what she's talking about. That summer Ali goes to the lake to spend the summer with her aunt and her cousin. This is the same lake her mom</span>
  <span id="freeText16392762956701935106" style="display:none">Deep Dark and Dangerous by Mary Downing Hahn is an excellent book if you're interested in paranormal books! It all started when the main character Ali was looking through her mom's old photographs. She finds a photo of her mother and siblings but then notices, there is someone ripped out of the photo. When Ali asks her mom, her mom acts as if she doesn't know what she's talking about. That summer Ali goes to the lake to spend the summer with her aunt and her cousin. This is the same lake her mom and family used to spend every summer at. One day she meets an usual little girl, the girl claims her name is Sissy. Sissy is not nice to Ali at all and is a bad influence on her cousin. Sissy tries to scare them by telling them about a story of a young girl,Theresa, who years ago drowned in the lake. Piece by piece Ali finds out that the ripped out girl in the photo is Sissy, also known as Theresa. This book is just to entertain the reader, it's a very exciting thriller! Deep Dark and Dangerous always keeps you on your toes from the beginning to end! Based on the description of the book above, if you enjoy a good, suspenseful book, I'd for sure recommend this book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16392762956701935106" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<li class='cover' id='bookCover_4857821'>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Z+tHiSwd3hb/J8HCMwnf9dL5GXIrrmDVQuk0dSYyj9Rsz/oFjT0d6gYoCOYrnVXPgzOBm1bebF7osfjR5Sosig==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('b1NHBmoemhjyfpzsBC7T9SAoweOaMZjhzgpannVQgKJkd/qKyz5Z5AtxVcgculnPceJZCudBlGpkUpY6tkgj/A==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

The place is New York City. Horace Carpetine has been raised to believe in science and rationality.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/10006.Mary_Downing_Hahn">About Mary Downing Hahn</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/10006.Mary_Downing_Hahn"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1208439316p3/10006.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/10006.Mary_Downing_Hahn">Mary Downing Hahn
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
2,664
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9715066383276208398">I grew up in a small shingled house down at the end of Guilford Road in College Park, Maryland. Our block was loaded with kids my age. We spent hours outdoors playing "Kick the Can" and "Mother, May I" as well as cowboy and outlaw games that usually ended in quarrels about who shot whom. In the summer, we went on day long expeditions into forbidden territory -- the woods on the other side of the t</span>
  <span id="freeText9715066383276208398" style="display:none">I grew up in a small shingled house down at the end of Guilford Road in College Park, Maryland. Our block was loaded with kids my age. We spent hours outdoors playing "Kick the Can" and "Mother, May I" as well as cowboy and outlaw games that usually ended in quarrels about who shot whom. In the summer, we went on day long expeditions into forbidden territory -- the woods on the other side of the train tracks, the creek that wound its way through College Park, and the experimental farm run by the University of Maryland.<br /><br />In elementary school, I was known as the class artist. I loved to read and draw but I hated writing reports. Requirements such as outlines, perfect penmanship, and following directions killed my interest in putting words on paper. All those facts -- who cared what the principal products of Chile were? To me, writing reports was almost as boring as math. <br /><br />Despite my dislike of writing, I loved to make up stories. Instead of telling them in words, I told them in pictures. My stories were usually about orphans who ran away and had the sort of exciting adventures I would have enjoyed if my mother hadn't always interfered.<br /><br />When I was in junior high school, I developed an interest in more complex stories. I wanted to show how people felt, what they thought, what they said. For this, I needed words. Although I wasn't sure I was smart enough, I decided to write and illustrate children's books when I grew up. Consequently, at the age of thirteen, I began my first book. Small Town Life was about a girl named Susan, as tall and skinny and freckle faced as I was. Unlike her shy, self conscious creator, however, Susan was a leader who lived the life I wanted to live -- my ideal self, in other words. Although I never finished Small Town Life, it marked the start of a lifelong interest in writing.<br /><br />In high school, I kept a diary. In college, I wrote poetry and short stories and dreamed of being published in The New Yorker. Unfortunately, I didn't have the courage or the confidence to send anything there. <br /><br />By the time my first novel was published, I was 41 years old. That's how long it took me to get serious about writing. The Sara Summer took me a year to write, another year to find a publisher, and yet another year of revisions before Clarion accepted it.<br /><br />Since Sara appeared in 1979, I've written an average of one book a year. If I have a plot firmly in mind when I begin, the writing goes fairly quickly. More typically, I start with a character or a situation and only a vague idea of what's going to happen. Therefore, I spend a lot of time revising and thinking things out. If I'd paid more attention to the craft of outlining back in elementary school, I might be a faster writer, but, on the other hand, if I knew everything that was going to happen in a story, I might be too bored to write it down. Writing is a journey of discovery. That's what makes it so exciting.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9715066383276208398" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
